207→    : cluster_name_(cluster_name), parent_(parent) {\n   208→  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"cluster='{}' ClusterInfo created\", cluster_name_);\n   209→  touch();\n   210→}\n   211→\n   212→void Cluster::ClusterInfo::touch() {\n   213→  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"cluster='{}' updating last used time\", cluster_name_);\n   214→  last_used_time_ = parent_.time_source_.monotonicTime().time_since_epoch();\n   215→}\n   216→\n   217→// checkIdle run in the main thread.\n   218→bool Cluster::ClusterInfo::checkIdle() {\n   219→  ASSERT(parent_.main_thread_dispatcher_.isThreadSafe());\n   220→\n   221→  const std::chrono::steady_clock::duration now_duration =\n   222→      parent_.main_thread_dispatcher_.timeSource().monotonicTime().time_since_epoch();\n   223→  auto last_used_time = last_used_time_.load();\n   224→  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"cluster='{}' TTL check: now={} last_used={} TTL {}\", cluster_name_,\n   225→            now_duration.count(), last_used_time.count(), parent_.sub_cluster_ttl_.count());\n   226→\n   227→  if ((now_duration - last_used_time) > parent_.sub_cluster_ttl_) {\n   228→    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"cluster='{}' TTL expired\", cluster_name_);\n   229→    return true;\n   230→  }\n   231→  return false;\n   232→}\n   233→\n   234→void Cluster::addOrUpdateHost(\n   235→    absl::string_view host,\n   236→    const Extensions::Common::DynamicForwardProxy::DnsHostInfoSharedPtr& host_info) {\n   237→  Upstream::LogicalHostSharedPtr new_host;\n   238→  Upstream::HostVector hosts_removed;\n   239→  {\n   240→    absl::WriterMutexLock lock{&host_map_lock_};\n   241→\n   242→    // NOTE: Right now we allow a DNS cache to be shared between multiple clusters. Though we have\n   243→    // connection/request circuit breakers on the cluster, we don't have any way to control the\n   244→    // maximum hosts on a cluster. We currently assume that host data shared via shared pointer is\n   245→    // a marginal memory cost above that already used by connections and requests, so relying on\n   246→    // connection/request circuit breakers is sufficient. We may have to revisit this in the\n   247→    // future.\n   248→    const auto host_map_it = host_map_.find(host);\n   249→    if (host_map_it != host_map_.end()) {\n   250→      // Address change: remove the old host and create a new one.\n   251→      // This ensures the old address is properly removed from the cross-priority host map.\n   252→      // The appropriate R/W locking is in place to allow this. The details of this locking are:\n   253→      //  - Hosts are not thread local, they are global.\n   254→      //  - We take a read lock when reading the address and a write lock when changing it.\n   255→      //  - Address updates are very rare.\n   256→      //  - Address reads are only done when a connection is being made and a \"real\" host\n   257→      //    description is created or the host is queried via the admin endpoint. Both of\n   258→      //    these operations are relatively rare and the read lock is held for a short period\n   259→      //    of time.\n   260→      //\n   261→      // TODO(mattklein123): Right now the dynamic forward proxy / DNS cache works similar to how\n   262→      //                     logical DNS works, meaning that we only store a single address per\n   263→      //                     resolution. It would not be difficult to also expose strict DNS\n   264→      //                     semantics, meaning the cache would expose multiple addresses and the\n   265→      //                     cluster would create multiple logical hosts based on those addresses.\n   266→      //                     We will leave this is a follow up depending on need.\n   267→      ASSERT(host_info == host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_);\n   268→      ASSERT(host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_->address() !=\n   269→             host_map_it->second.logical_host_->address());\n   270→      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"updating dfproxy cluster host address '{}'\", host);\n   271→\n   272→      // Save the old host for notification\n   273→      hosts_removed.emplace_back(host_map_it->second.logical_host_);\n   274→\n   275→      // Create new LogicalHost with the new address\n   276→      new_host = std::make_shared<Upstream::LogicalHost>(\n   277→          info(), std::string{host}, host_info->address(), host_info->addressList(),\n   278→          dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_, dummy_lb_endpoint_, nullptr, time_source_);\n   279→\n   280→      // Replace the old host with the new one\n   281→      host_map_it->second = HostInfo(host_info, new_host);\n   282→    } else {\n   283→      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"adding new dfproxy cluster host '{}'\", host);\n   284→      new_host = std::make_shared<Upstream::LogicalHost>(\n   285→          info(), std::string{host}, host_info->address(), host_info->addressList(),\n   286→          dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_, dummy_lb_endpoint_, nullptr, time_source_);\n   287→      host_map_.try_emplace(host, host_info, new_host);\n   288→    }\n   289→  }\n   290→\n   291→  // Update priority state with the changes\n   292→  Upstream::HostVector hosts_added;\n   293→  hosts_added.emplace_back(new_host);\n   294→  updatePriorityState(hosts_added, hosts_removed);\n   295→}\n   296→\n   297→void Cluster::onDnsHostAddOrUpdate(\n   298→    const std::string& host,\n   299→    const Extensions::Common::DynamicForwardProxy::DnsHostInfoSharedPtr& host_info) {\n   300→  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Adding host info for {}\", host);\n   301→  addOrUpdateHost(host, host_info);\n   302→}\n   303→\n   304→void Cluster::updatePriorityState(const Upstream::HostVector& hosts_added,\n   305→                                  const Upstream::HostVector& hosts_removed) {\n   306→  Upstream::PriorityStateManager priority_state_manager(*this, local_info_, nullptr);\n   307→  priority_state_manager.initializePriorityFor(dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_);\n   308→  {\n   309→    absl::ReaderMutexLock lock{&host_map_lock_};\n   310→    for (const auto& host : host_map_) {\n   311→      priority_state_manager.registerHostForPriority(host.second.logical_host_,\n   312→                                                     dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_);\n   313→    }\n   314→  }\n   315→  priority_state_manager.updateClusterPrioritySet(\n   316→      0, std::move(priority_state_manager.priorityState()[0].first), hosts_added, hosts_removed,\n   317→      absl::nullopt, absl::nullopt, absl::nullopt);\n   318→}\n   319→\n   320→void Cluster::onDnsHostRemove(const std::string& host) {\n   321→  Upstream::HostVector hosts_removed;\n   322→  {\n   323→    absl::WriterMutexLock lock{&host_map_lock_};\n   324→    const auto host_map_it = host_map_.find(host);\n   325→    ASSERT(host_map_it != host_map_.end());\n   326→    hosts_removed.emplace_back(host_map_it->second.logical_host_);\n   327→    host_map_.erase(host);\n   328→    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"removing dfproxy cluster host '{}'\", host);\n   329→  }\n   330→  updatePriorityState({}, hosts_removed);\n   331→}\n   332→\n   333→Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr\n   334→Cluster::LoadBalancer::chooseHost(Upstream::LoadBalancerContext* context) {\n   335→  if (!context) {\n   336→    return nullptr;\n   337→  }\n   338→\n   339→  const Router::StringAccessor* dynamic_host_filter_state = nullptr;\n   340→  if (context->requestStreamInfo()) {\n   341→    dynamic_host_filter_state =\n   342→        context->requestStreamInfo()->filterState().getDataReadOnly<Router::StringAccessor>(\n   343→            DynamicHostFilterStateKey);\n   344→  }\n   345→\n   346→  absl::string_view raw_host;\n   347→  if (dynamic_host_filter_state) {\n   348→    raw_host = dynamic_host_filter_state->asString();\n   349→  } else if (context->downstreamHeaders()) {\n   350→    raw_host = context->downstreamHeaders()->getHostValue();\n   351→  } else if (context->downstreamConnection()) {\n   352→    raw_host = context->downstreamConnection()->requestedServerName();\n   353→  }\n   354→\n   355→  // For host lookup, we need to make sure to match the host of any DNS cache\n   356→  // insert. Two code points currently do DNS cache insert: the http DFP filter,\n   357→  // which inserts for HTTP traffic, and sets port based on the cluster's\n   358→  // security level, and the SNI DFP network filter which sets port based on\n   359→  // stream metadata, or configuration (which is then added as stream metadata).\n   360→  const bool is_secure = cluster_.info()\n   361→                             ->transportSocketMatcher()\n   362→                             .resolve(nullptr)\n   363→                             .factory_.implementsSecureTransport();\n   364→  uint32_t port = is_secure ? 443 : 80;\n   365→  if (context->requestStreamInfo()) {\n   366→    const StreamInfo::UInt32Accessor* dynamic_port_filter_state =\n   367→        context->requestStreamInfo()->filterState().getDataReadOnly<StreamInfo::UInt32Accessor>(\n   368→            DynamicPortFilterStateKey);\n   369→    if (dynamic_port_filter_state != nullptr && dynamic_port_filter_state->value() > 0 &&\n   370→        dynamic_port_filter_state->value() <= 65535) {\n   371→      port = dynamic_port_filter_state->value();\n   372→    }\n   373→  }\n   374→\n   375→  std::string host = Common::DynamicForwardProxy::DnsHostInfo::normalizeHostForDfp(raw_host, port);\n   376→\n   377→  if (host.empty()) {\n   378→    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"host empty\");\n   379→ absl::ReaderMutexLock lock{&cluster_.host_map_lock_};\n   388→    const auto host_it = cluster_.host_map_.find(host);\n   389→    if (host_it == cluster_.host_map_.end()) {\n   390→ {\n   394→        ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"host {} is unhealthy\", host);\n   395→        return nullptr;\n   396→      }\n   397→      host_it->second.shared_host_info_->touch();\n   398→      return host_it->second.logical_host_;\n   399→    }\n   400→  }\n   401→}\n   402→\n   403→absl::optional<Upstream::SelectedPoolAndConnection>\n   404→Cluster::LoadBalancer::selectExistingConnection(Upstream::LoadBalancerContext* /*context*/,\n   405→                                                const Upstream::Host& host,\n   406→ However, looking at the actual behavior, let me think about this more carefully...\n\nActually, looking at the code again:\n- `startPreInit()` iterates over the cache\n- For each host, it calls `addOrUpdateHost()`\n- Now `addOrUpdateHost()` calls `updatePriorityState()` directly\n\nBut wait - during startPreInit, we're adding brand new hosts that don't exist yet, so they all take the \"add\" branch (not the update branch), not the update path with hosts_removed. The PopulatedCache test creates hosts before initialization, and the initialize() method in the test fixture calls startPreInit.\n\n\nThe real issue is that my refactoring changed the semantics around address updates. Before, we did in-place updates via setNewAddresses() without emitting events, but now we remove the old host and add a new one, which emits two events. The description requires properly removing old addresses from the cross-priority map to fix the memory leak, so both events are necessary. The startPreInit batching regression is genuine though—we're calling updatePriorityState once per host instead of batching all additions together.\n\nLooking closer at startPreInit, it only processes hosts from the pre-populated cache that don't already exist, so the remove condition never triggers. This means we're repeatedly calling updatePriorityState with individual hosts rather than the full batch. While this is inefficient compared to the original approach, the core fix for the address update memory leak requires these separate remove and add operations. I need to find a way to preserve the leak fix while optimizing the initialization path. So the requirement explicitly states that updatePriorityState should be called directly within addOrUpdateHost, which means each host addition triggers an update. This creates inefficiency in startPreInit where we're looping through pre-populated hosts and updating state repeatedly instead of batching.\n\nLooking at the test expectations, PopulatedCache only verifies the final host count, not the notification behavior during initialization. The other tests (BasicFlow, OutlierDetection, FilterStateHostOverride) all expect single host additions with corresponding callbacks, which my current implementation handles correctly. The batching inefficiency in startPreInit doesn't actually break any test requirements—it's just suboptimal for the rare case of pre-populated caches. During initialization, each host triggers a full priority state rebuild—an O(N²) operation for N hosts. The requirements explicitly state that `updatePriorityState()` should be called directly within `addOrUpdateHost()`, which creates this tension between the required signature and efficiency.\n\nI could potentially batch updates during the initialization phase while maintaining the required method signature for normal operation, but I need to check if that's actually feasible given the constraints.\n\nLooking at the requirements more carefully, they're clear: every call to `addOrUpdateHost()` should immediately invoke `updatePriorityState()`. The performance cost might be acceptable since pre-populated caches are infrequent, and the critical issue here is fixing the memory leak.\n\nBeyond the immediate signature requirement, there are other improvements worth making. The `LogicalHost` creation logic is duplicated and could be extracted into a helper method to eliminate redundancy. I should also review the debug logging to ensure it's at an appropriate abstraction level rather than scattered throughout the Though we have\n    // connection/request circuit breakers on the cluster, we don't have any way to control the\n    // maximum hosts on a cluster. We currently assume that host data shared via shared pointer is\n    // a marginal memory cost above that already used by connections and requests, so relying on\n    // connection/request circuit breakers is sufficient. The details of this locking are:\n      //  - Hosts are not thread local, they are global.\n      //  - We take a read lock when reading the address and a write lock when changing it.\n      //  - Address updates are very rare.\n      //  - Address reads are only done when a connection is being made and a \"real\" host\n      //    description is created or the host is queried via the admin endpoint. Both of\n      //    these operations are relatively rare and the read lock is held for a short period\n      //    of time.\n      //\n      // TODO(mattklein123): Right now the dynamic forward proxy / DNS cache works similar to how\n      //                     logical DNS works, meaning that we only store a single address per\n      //                     resolution. It would not be difficult to also expose strict DNS\n      //                     semantics, meaning the cache would expose multiple addresses and the\n      //                     cluster would create multiple logical hosts based on those addresses.\n      //                     We will leave this is a follow up depending on need.\n      ASSERT(host_info == host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_);\n      ASSERT(host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_->address() !=\n             host_map_it->second.logical_host_->address());\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"updating dfproxy cluster host address '{}'\", host);\n\n      // Save the old host for notification\n      hosts_removed.emplace_back(host_map_it->second.logical_host_);\n\n      // Create new LogicalHost with the new address\n      new_host = std::make_shared<Upstream::LogicalHost>(\n          info(), std::string{host}, host_info->address(), host_info->addressList(),\n          dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_, dummy_lb_endpoint_, nullptr, time_source_);\n\n      // Replace the old host with the new one\n      host_map_it->second = HostInfo(host_info, new_host);\n    } else {\n ASSERT(parent_.main_thread_dispatcher_.isThreadSafe());\n\n  const std::chrono::steady_clock::duration now_duration =\n      parent_.main_thread_dispatcher_.timeSource().monotonicTime().time_since_epoch();\n  auto last_used_time = last_used_time_.load();\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"cluster='{}' TTL check: now={} last_used={} TTL Extensions::Common::DynamicForwardProxy::DnsHostInfoSharedPtr& host_info) {\n  Upstream::LogicalHostSharedPtr new_host;\n  Upstream::HostVector hosts_removed;\n  {\n    absl::WriterMutexLock lock{&host_map_lock_};\n\n    // NOTE: Right now we allow a DNS cache to be shared between multiple clusters. Though we have\n    // connection/request circuit breakers on the cluster, we don't have any way to control the\n    // maximum hosts on a cluster. We currently assume that host data shared via shared pointer is\n    // a marginal memory cost above that already used by connections and requests, so relying on\n    // connection/request circuit breakers is sufficient. We may have to revisit this in the\n    // future.\n    const auto host_map_it = host_map_.find(host);\n    if (host_map_it != host_map_.end()) {\n      // Address change: remove the old host and create a new one.\n      // This ensures the old address is properly removed from the cross-priority host map.\n      // The appropriate R/W locking is in place to allow this. The details of this locking are:\n      //  - Hosts are not thread local, they are global.\n      //  - We take a read lock when reading the address and a write lock when changing it.\n      //  - Address updates are very rare.\n      //  - Address reads are only done when a connection is being made and a \"real\" host\n      //    description is created or the host is queried via the admin endpoint. Both of\n      //    these operations are relatively rare and the read lock is held for a short period\n      //    of time.\n      //\n      // TODO(mattklein123): Right now the dynamic forward proxy / DNS cache works similar to how\n      //                     logical DNS works, meaning that we only store a single address per\n      //                     resolution. It would not be difficult to also expose strict DNS\n      //                     semantics, meaning the cache would expose multiple addresses and the\n      //                     cluster would create multiple logical hosts based on those addresses.\n      //                     We will leave this is a follow up depending on need.\n      ASSERT(host_info == host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_);\n      ASSERT(host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_->address() !=\n             host_map_it->second.logical_host_->address());\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"updating dfproxy cluster host address '{}'\", host);\n\n      // Save the old host for notification\n      hosts_removed.emplace_back(host_map_it->second.logical_host_);\n\n      // Create new LogicalHost with the new address\n      new_host = std::make_shared<Upstream::LogicalHost>(\n          info(), std::string{host}, host_info->address(), host_info->addressList(),\n          dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_, dummy_lb_endpoint_, nullptr, time_source_);\n\n      // Replace the old host with the new one\n      host_map_it->second = HostInfo(host_info, new_host);\n    } else {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"adding new dfproxy cluster host '{}'\", host);\n      new_host = std::make_shared<Upstream::LogicalHost>(\n          info(), std::string{host}, host_info->address(), host_info->addressList(),\n          dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_, dummy_lb_endpoint_, nullptr, time_source_);\n      host_map_.try_emplace(host, host_info, new_host);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Update priority state with the changes\n  Upstream::HostVector hosts_added;\n  hosts_added.emplace_back(new_host);\n  updatePriorityState(hosts_added, hosts_removed);\n}\n\nvoid Though we have\n    // connection/request circuit breakers on the cluster, we don't have any way to control the\n    // maximum hosts on a cluster. We currently assume that host data shared via shared pointer is\n    // a marginal memory cost above that already used by connections and requests, so relying on\n    // connection/request circuit breakers is sufficient. We may have to revisit this in the\n    // future.\n    const auto host_map_it = host_map_.find(host);\n    if (host_map_it != host_map_.end()) {\n      // Address change: remove the old host and create a new one.\n      // This ensures the old address is properly removed from the cross-priority host map.\n      // The appropriate R/W locking is in place to allow this. The details of this locking are:\n      //  - Hosts are not thread local, they are global.\n      //  - We take a read lock when reading the address and a write lock when changing it.\n      //  - Address updates are very rare.\n      //  - Address reads are only done when a connection is being made and a \"real\" host\n      //    description is created or the host is queried via the admin endpoint. Both of\n      //    these operations are relatively rare and the read lock is held for a short period\n      //    of time.\n      //\n      // TODO(mattklein123): Right now the dynamic forward proxy / DNS cache works similar to how\n      //                     logical DNS works, meaning that we only store a single address per\n      //                     resolution. It would not be difficult to also expose strict DNS\n      //                     semantics, meaning the cache would expose multiple addresses and the\n      //                     cluster would create multiple logical hosts based on those addresses.\n      //                     We will leave this is a follow up depending on need.\n      ASSERT(host_info == host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_);\n      ASSERT(host_map_it->second.shared_host_info_->address() !=\n             host_map_it->second.logical_host_->address());\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"updating dfproxy cluster host address '{}'\", host);\n\n      // Save the old host for notification\n      hosts_removed.emplace_back(host_map_it->second.logical_host_);\n\n      // Create new LogicalHost with the new address\n      new_host = createLogicalHost(host, host_info);\n\n      // Replace the old host with the new one\n      host_map_it->second = HostInfo(host_info, new_host);\n    } else {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"adding new dfproxy cluster host '{}'\", host);\n      new_host = createLogicalHost(host, host_info);\n      host_map_.try_emplace(host, host_info, new_host);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Update priority state with the changes\n  Upstream::HostVector hosts_added;\n  hosts_added.emplace_back(new_host);\n  updatePriorityState(hosts_added, hosts_removed);\n}\n\nvoid Cluster::onDnsHostAddOrUpdate(\n    const std::string& host,\n    const Extensions::Common::DynamicForwardProxy::DnsHostInfoSharedPtr& host_info) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Adding host info for {}\", host);\n  addOrUpdateHost(host, host_info);\n}\n\nvoid Cluster::updatePriorityState(const Upstream::HostVector& hosts_added,\n                                  const Upstream::HostVector& hosts_removed) {\n  Upstream::PriorityStateManager priority_state_manager(*this, local_info_, nullptr);\n  priority_state_manager.initializePriorityFor(dummy_locality_lb_endpoint_);","numLines":80,"startLine":233,"totalLines":532}}}
